105→import static org.apache.kafka.connect.runtime.ConnectorConfig.VALUE_CONVERTER_VERSION_CONFIG;\n   106→\n   107→\n   108→/**\n   109→ * Abstract Herder implementation which handles connector/task lifecycle tracking. Extensions\n   110→ * must invoke the lifecycle hooks appropriately.\n   111→ * <p>\n   112→ * This class takes the following approach for sending status updates to the backing store:\n   113→ *\n   114→ * <ol>\n   115→ * <li>\n   116→ *    When the connector or task is starting, we overwrite the previous state blindly. This ensures that\n   117→ *    every rebalance will reset the state of tasks to the proper state. The intuition is that there should\n   118→ *    be less chance of write conflicts when the worker has just received its assignment and is starting tasks.\n   119→ *    In particular, this prevents us from depending on the generation absolutely. If the group disappears\n   120→ *    and the generation is reset, then we'll overwrite the status information with the older (and larger)\n   121→ *    generation with the updated one. The danger of this approach is that slow starting tasks may cause the\n   122→ *    status to be overwritten after a rebalance has completed.\n   123→ *\n   124→ * <li>\n   125→ *    If the connector or task fails or is shutdown, we use {@link StatusBackingStore#putSafe(ConnectorStatus)},\n   126→ *    which provides a little more protection if the worker is no longer in the group (in which case the\n   127→ *    task may have already been started on another worker). Extensions\n * must invoke the lifecycle hooks appropriately.\n * <p>\n * This class takes the following approach for sending status updates to the backing store:\n *\n * <ol>\n * <li>\n *    When the connector or task is starting, we overwrite the previous state blindly. This ensures that\n *    every rebalance will reset the state of tasks to the proper state. The intuition is that there should\n *    be less chance of write conflicts when the worker has just received its assignment and is starting tasks.\n *    In particular, this prevents us from depending on the generation absolutely. If the group disappears\n *    and the generation is reset, then we'll overwrite the status information with the older (and larger)\n *    generation with the updated one. The danger of this approach is that slow starting tasks may cause the\n *    status to be overwritten after a rebalance has completed.\n *\n * <li>\n *    If the connector or task fails or is shutdown, we use {@link StatusBackingStore#putSafe(ConnectorStatus)},\n *    which provides a little more protection if the worker is no longer in the group (in which case the\n *    task may have already been started on another worker). Obviously this is still racy. If the task has just\n *    started on another worker, we may not have the updated status cached yet. In this case, we'll overwrite\n *    the value which will cause the state to be inconsistent (most likely until the next rebalance). Until\n *    we have proper producer groups with fenced groups, there is not much else we can do.\n * </ol>\n */\npublic abstract class AbstractHerder implements Herder, TaskStatus.Listener, ConnectorStatus.Listener {\n\n    private static final Logger log = LoggerFactory.getLogger(AbstractHerder.class);\n\n    private final String workerId;\n    protected final Worker worker;\n    private final String kafkaClusterId;\n    protected final StatusBackingStore statusBackingStore;\n    protected final ConfigBackingStore configBackingStore;\n    private volatile boolean ready = false;\n    private final Plugin<ConnectorClientConfigOverridePolicy> connectorClientConfigOverridePolicyPlugin;\n    private final ExecutorService connectorExecutor;\n    private final Time time;\n    protected final Loggers loggers;\n\n    private final CachedConnectors cachedConnectors;\n\n    public AbstractHerder(Worker worker,","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1287}}}

Most importantly, this includes writing updated configurations for connectors and tasks,\n *     (and therefore, also for creating, destroy, and scaling up/down connectors).\n * </p>\n * <p>\n *     The DistributedHerder uses a single thread for most of its processing. This includes processing\n *     config changes, handling task rebalances and serving requests from the HTTP layer. The latter are pushed\n *     into a queue until the thread has time to handle them. A consequence of this is that requests can get blocked\n *     behind a worker rebalance. When the herder knows that a rebalance is expected, it typically returns an error","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":3035}}}

Let me compile the complete list of files that implement the service initialization lifecycle pattern. Based on my investigation, I found:\n\n1. **Key Lifecycle Interfaces:**\n   - `Herder.java` - interface with start()/stop()\n   - `ConfigBackingStore.java` - interface with start()/stop()\n   - `StatusBackingStore.java` - interface with start()/stop()\n   - `OffsetBackingStore.java` - interface with start()\n   - `Scheduler.java` - interface with startup()/shutdown()\n   - `NodeToControllerChannelManager.java` - interface with start()/shutdown()\n   - `Persister.java` - interface with stop()\n   - `RestServer.java` - abstract class with stop()\n\n2. **Key Implementation Classes:**\n   - `AbstractHerder.java` - implements Herder, manages startServices()/stopServices()\n   - `DistributedHerder.java` - extends AbstractHerder, implements distributed startup/shutdown\n   - `StandaloneHerder.java` - extends AbstractHerder, standalone implementation\n   - `Connect.java` - orchestrates Herder and RestServer lifecycle\n   - `Worker.java` - implements Worker interface with start()/stop()\n   - `AbstractWorkerSourceTask.java` - implements WorkerSourceTask with stop()\n   - `WorkerSinkTask.java` - implements SinkTask with stop()\n   - `WorkerTask.java` - implements Task with stop()\n   - `WorkerConnector.java` - implements Connector with shutdown()\n   - `ConnectMetrics.java` - manages metrics with stop()\n   - `KafkaConfigBackingStore.java` - implements ConfigBackingStore\n   - `KafkaStatusBackingStore.java` - implements StatusBackingStore\n   - `KafkaOffsetBackingStore.java` - implements OffsetBackingStore\n   - `ConnectorOffsetBackingStore.java` - implements OffsetBackingStore\n   - `MemoryConfigBackingStore.java` - implements ConfigBackingStore\n   - `MemoryStatusBackingStore.java` - implements StatusBackingStore\n   - `MemoryOffsetBackingStore.java` - implements OffsetBackingStore\n   - `KafkaScheduler.java` - implements Scheduler\n   - `DefaultStatePersister.java` - implements Persister\n   - `NoOpStatePersister.java` - implements Persister\n   - Apache Kafka\\n\\nApache Kafka implements a comprehensive Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle pattern across its Connect runtime, server, and client modules. The pattern ensures coordinated startup and shutdown of dependent services in reverse order.\\n\\n## Core Lifecycle Interfaces\\n\\nThe primary interfaces defining the lifecycle pattern are:\\n\\n1. **Herder Interface** (connect/runtime/Herder.java) - Manages worker and connector lifecycle with start() and stop() methods\\n2. **ConfigBackingStore Interface** (connect/runtime/storage/ConfigBackingStore.java) - Handles connector configuration persistence with start() and stop()\\n3. **StatusBackingStore Interface** (connect/runtime/storage/StatusBackingStore.java) - Tracks connector and task status with start() and stop()\\n4. **OffsetBackingStore Interface** (connect/runtime/storage/OffsetBackingStore.java) - Manages source connector offsets with start() and stop()\\n5. **Scheduler Interface** (server-common/util/Scheduler.java) - Schedules background tasks with startup() and shutdown()\\n6. **NodeToControllerChannelManager Interface** (server-common/NodeToControllerChannelManager.java) - Manages broker-to-controller communication with start() and shutdown()\\n7. **Persister Interface** (server-common/persister/Persister.java) - Persists share group state with stop()\\n\\n## Service Startup and Shutdown Ordering\\n\\nThe **AbstractHerder** class (connect/runtime/AbstractHerder.java) implements the core lifecycle coordination pattern:\\n\\n### Startup Order (AbstractHerder.startServices()):\\n1. worker.start() - Initialize the Worker component\\n2. statusBackingStore.start() - Start the status backing store\\n3. configBackingStore.start() - Start the configuration backing store\\n\\n### Shutdown Order (AbstractHerder.stopServices()) - REVERSE ORDER:\\n1. statusBackingStore.stop() - Stop status store first\\n2. configBackingStore.stop() - Stop config store second\\n3. worker.stop() - Stop worker last\\n4. connectorExecutor.shutdown() - Shutdown connector executor\\n5. connectorClientConfigOverridePolicyPlugin.close() - Close policy plugin\\n\\nThis reverse-order shutdown ensures that dependent services are properly cleaned up before their dependencies are stopped, preventing resource leaks and data loss.\\n\\n## Key Implementation Classes\\n\\n### Herder Implementations\\n- **DistributedHerder** (connect/runtime/distributed/DistributedHerder.java) - Manages distributed Kafka Connect clusters with coordinated service startup, heartbeat handling, and graceful shutdown\\n- **StandaloneHerder** (connect/runtime/standalone/StandaloneHerder.java) - Simplified standalone implementation for single-process Kafka Connect\\n\\n### Storage Backing Store Implementations\\n- **KafkaConfigBackingStore** - Stores connector configurations in Kafka topics\\n- **KafkaStatusBackingStore** - Tracks connector/task status in Kafka topics\\n- **KafkaOffsetBackingStore** - Maintains source connector offsets in Kafka\\n- **MemoryConfigBackingStore** - In-memory configuration storage for standalone mode\\n- **MemoryStatusBackingStore** - In-memory status tracking for standalone mode\\n- **MemoryOffsetBackingStore** - In-memory offset tracking for standalone mode\\n\\n### Worker and Task Lifecycle\\n- **Worker** (connect/runtime/Worker.java) - Manages connector and task execution with coordinated start/stop\\n- **WorkerConnector** - Manages individual connector lifecycle\\n- **WorkerTask**, **WorkerSinkTask**, **AbstractWorkerSourceTask** - Manage individual task lifecycle\\n- **ConnectMetrics** - Manages metrics lifecycle with proper cleanup on stop\\n\\n### Scheduler Implementations\\n- **KafkaScheduler** (server-common/util/KafkaScheduler.java) - Manages scheduled background tasks with startup() and graceful shutdown()\\n\\n### State Persistence\\n- **DefaultStatePersister** - Implements share group state persistence\\n- **NoOpStatePersister** - No-op implementation for share group persistence\\n- **PersisterStateManager** - Manages persister lifecycle\\n\\n## Orchestration Layer\\n\\nThe **Connect** class (connect/runtime/Connect.java) serves as the top-level orchestrator, managing the complete lifecycle of the Kafka Connect process:\\n\\n```\\nConnect.start():\\n  1. Exit.addShutdownHook()\\n  2. herder.start()\\n  3. rest.initializeResources()\\n\\nConnect.stop():\\n  1. rest.stop()\\n  2. herder.stop()\\n```\\n\\nThis ensures the REST server is stopped before the herder, which manages all running connectors and their dependent services.\\n\\n## Lifecycle Characteristics\\n\\n1. **Coordinated Initialization**: Services are started in dependency order to ensure all prerequisites are available\\n2. **Reverse Shutdown Order**: Services stop in reverse initialization order, preventing dependency issues during shutdown\\n3. **Graceful Termination**: Timeout-based shutdown with configurable grace periods for task and connector shutdown\\n4. **State Consistency**: Configuration and status backing stores coordinate to maintain consistent state across cluster\\n5. **Error Handling**: Comprehensive error handling with proper cleanup in exceptional cases (see DistributedHerder.run() try-finally block)\\n\\nThis pattern ensures reliable and predictable service initialization and shutdown sequences in a distributed system, which is critical for Kafka Connect's role as a data integration platform.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3338,"cache_read_input_tokens":67618,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3338},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5892aa8a-7ff4-41a4-b6f3-e99f59a4413d","uuid":"13fa1789-041e-491b-a960-2e0f6e299ce7"}

Apache Kafka\\n\\nApache Kafka implements a comprehensive Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle pattern across its Connect runtime, server, and client modules. The pattern ensures coordinated startup and shutdown of dependent services in reverse order.\\n\\n## Core Lifecycle Interfaces\\n\\nThe primary interfaces defining the lifecycle pattern are:\\n\\n1. **Herder Interface** (connect/runtime/Herder.java) - Manages worker and connector lifecycle with start() and stop() methods\\n2. **ConfigBackingStore Interface** (connect/runtime/storage/ConfigBackingStore.java) - Handles connector configuration persistence with start() and stop()\\n3. **StatusBackingStore Interface** (connect/runtime/storage/StatusBackingStore.java) - Tracks connector and task status with start() and stop()\\n4. **OffsetBackingStore Interface** (connect/runtime/storage/OffsetBackingStore.java) - Manages source connector offsets with start() and stop()\\n5. **Scheduler Interface** (server-common/util/Scheduler.java) - Schedules background tasks with startup() and shutdown()\\n6. **NodeToControllerChannelManager Interface** (server-common/NodeToControllerChannelManager.java) - Manages broker-to-controller communication with start() and shutdown()\\n7. **Persister Interface** (server-common/persister/Persister.java) - Persists share group state with stop()\\n\\n## Service Startup and Shutdown Ordering\\n\\nThe **AbstractHerder** class (connect/runtime/AbstractHerder.java) implements the core lifecycle coordination pattern:\\n\\n### Startup Order (AbstractHerder.startServices()):\\n1. worker.start() - Initialize the Worker component\\n2. statusBackingStore.start() - Start the status backing store\\n3. configBackingStore.start() - Start the configuration backing store\\n\\n### Shutdown Order (AbstractHerder.stopServices()) - REVERSE ORDER:\\n1. statusBackingStore.stop() - Stop status store first\\n2. configBackingStore.stop() - Stop config store second\\n3. worker.stop() - Stop worker last\\n4. connectorExecutor.shutdown() - Shutdown connector executor\\n5. connectorClientConfigOverridePolicyPlugin.close() - Close policy plugin\\n\\nThis reverse-order shutdown ensures that dependent services are properly cleaned up before their dependencies are stopped, preventing resource leaks and data loss.\\n\\n## Key Implementation Classes\\n\\n### Herder Implementations\\n- **DistributedHerder** (connect/runtime/distributed/DistributedHerder.java) - Manages distributed Kafka Connect clusters with coordinated service startup, heartbeat handling, and graceful shutdown\\n- **StandaloneHerder** (connect/runtime/standalone/StandaloneHerder.java) - Simplified standalone implementation for single-process Kafka Connect\\n\\n### Storage Backing Store Implementations\\n- **KafkaConfigBackingStore** - Stores connector configurations in Kafka topics\\n- **KafkaStatusBackingStore** - Tracks connector/task status in Kafka topics\\n- **KafkaOffsetBackingStore** - Maintains source connector offsets in Kafka\\n- **MemoryConfigBackingStore** - In-memory configuration storage for standalone mode\\n- **MemoryStatusBackingStore** - In-memory status tracking for standalone mode\\n- **MemoryOffsetBackingStore** - In-memory offset tracking for standalone mode\\n\\n### Worker and Task Lifecycle\\n- **Worker** (connect/runtime/Worker.java) - Manages connector and task execution with coordinated start/stop\\n- **WorkerConnector** - Manages individual connector lifecycle\\n- **WorkerTask**, **WorkerSinkTask**, **AbstractWorkerSourceTask** - Manage individual task lifecycle\\n- **ConnectMetrics** - Manages metrics lifecycle with proper cleanup on stop\\n\\n### Scheduler Implementations\\n- **KafkaScheduler** (server-common/util/KafkaScheduler.java) - Manages scheduled background tasks with startup() and graceful shutdown()\\n\\n### State Persistence\\n- **DefaultStatePersister** - Implements share group state persistence\\n- **NoOpStatePersister** - No-op implementation for share group persistence\\n- **PersisterStateManager** - Manages persister lifecycle\\n\\n## Orchestration Layer\\n\\nThe **Connect** class (connect/runtime/Connect.java) serves as the top-level orchestrator, managing the complete lifecycle of the Kafka Connect process:\\n\\n```\\nConnect.start():\\n  1. Exit.addShutdownHook()\\n  2. herder.start()\\n  3. rest.initializeResources()\\n\\nConnect.stop():\\n  1. rest.stop()\\n  2. herder.stop()\\n```\\n\\nThis ensures the REST server is stopped before the herder, which manages all running connectors and their dependent services.\\n\\n## Lifecycle Characteristics\\n\\n1. **Coordinated Initialization**: Services are started in dependency order to ensure all prerequisites are available\\n2. **Reverse Shutdown Order**: Services stop in reverse initialization order, preventing dependency issues during shutdown\\n3. **Graceful Termination**: Timeout-based shutdown with configurable grace periods for task and connector shutdown\\n4. **State Consistency**: Configuration and status backing stores coordinate to maintain consistent state across cluster\\n5. **Error Handling**: Comprehensive error handling with proper cleanup in exceptional cases (see DistributedHerder.run() try-finally block)\\n\\nThis pattern ensures reliable and predictable service initialization and shutdown sequences in a distributed system, which is critical for Kafka Connect's role as a data integration platform.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
